Then RMSNorm is also in float.\n\nFor the fused kernel, to match the reference with acceptable tolerance:\n- Load all-reduced value (already in `tA` as bf16)\n- Load residual\n- Convert both to float, add\n- Store sum back to `tA` (as bf16) and write to residual_out (as bf16)\n- Accumulate sum of squares in float\n- After denom compute, load from `tA` (as bf16), convert to float, multiply by denom and weight, convert back to bf16, store to output\n\nThis is how the reference does it. Let me also note that `qr_to_float` and `qr_from_float` are available.\n\nActually, looking at `qr_to_float` and `qr_from_float`, they do individual element conversion. For better performance I could use vectorized operations, but for simplicity and correctness, let me use the scalar conversions.\n\nNow let me write the actual implementation. I need to handle the shared memory for row sums.\n\nThe access pattern to `weight[col_in_row]` might be slow. Let me think about caching weights. For hidden_dim=4096 and 256 threads, each warp (64 threads) accesses 64 consecutive columns, which is coalesced. The next warp accesses columns 64..127, also coalesced. So actually, the weight access is coalesced within each warp! Great.\n\nWait, let me verify: in the inner loop, for a fixed chunk i, thread t processes elements at columns:\n`col = (t*8 + i*2048) % hidden_dim`\n\nFor hidden_dim=4096 and i=0: col = t*8 .. t*8+7. Thread 0: 0..7, thread 1: 8..15, ..., thread 63: 504..511, thread 64: 512..519, etc.\nSo within a warp (threads 0..63), the columns are 0..511. These are contiguous, so coalesced access.\n\nActually, threads in a warp access 64 different 2-byte elements starting from 0, so 128 bytes total, which fits in 2-4 cache lines. The hardware handles this well.\n\nFor i=1: col = (t*8 + 2048) % 4096 = 2048 + t*8. Thread 0: 2048..2055, thread 1: 2056..2063, etc. Also coalesced.\n\nSo weight access is actually quite good!\n\nNow let me write the implementation properly:\n\n```cpp\n__device__ static void run(T const* __restrict__ input,\n                           T const* __restrict__ residual_inp,\n                           T* __restrict__ residual_out,\n                           T* __restrict__ output,\n                           T const* __restrict__ weight,\n                           float eps,\n                           uint32_t const N,\n                           uint32_t const hidden_dim,\n                           int const block,\n                           int const rank,\n                           uint8_t** __restrict__ buffer_list,\n                           uint32_t const data_offset,\n                           uint32_t flag_color,\n                           int64_t data_size_per_phase)\n{\n    int thread = threadIdx.x + threadIdx.y * kWavefront;\n    uint8_t* rank_buffer = buffer_list[rank];\n    Codec codec(thread, rank);\n    int block_id = blockIdx.x;\n    uint8_t* buffer_ptr[kWorldSize];\n    for(int i = 0; i < kWorldSize; ++i)\n    {\n        buffer_ptr[i] = buffer_list[i];\n    }\n\n    // --------------------------------------------------------\n    // Read input into registers\n    int32x4_t tA[kAtoms];\n\n    BufferResource src_buffer(const_cast<T*>(input), N * sizeof(T));\n    uint32_t src_offset = block * kTileSize + thread * sizeof(int32x4_t);\n\n    for(int i = 0; i < kAtoms; i++)\n    {\n        tA[i] = buffer_load_dwordx4(src_buffer.descriptor, src_offset, 0, 0);\n        src_offset += kAtomStride * sizeof(int32x4_t);\n        if constexpr(cast_bf2half)\n        {\n            const nv_bfloat162* bf_buf = reinterpret_cast<const nv_bfloat162*>(&tA[i]);\n            half2 half_buf[4];\n            #pragma unroll\n            for(int j = 0; j < 4; ++j)\n            {\n                float2 f    = __bfloat1622float2(bf_buf[j]);\n                half_buf[j] = __float22half2_rn(f);\n            }\n            tA[i] = *reinterpret_cast<const int32x4_t*>(half_buf);\n        }\n    }\n\n    // --------------------------------------------------------\n    // Phase-1A: Write segment data into the communication buffer of the target\n    // rank responsible for this segment.\n    uint32_t comm_data0_offset = data_offset + block_id * Codec::kTransmittedTileSize;\n    uint32_t comm_data1_offset = data_size_per_phase + comm_data0_offset;\n\n    uint32_t comm_flags0_offset = block_id * (kWorldSize * sizeof(uint32_t));\n    uint32_t comm_flags1_offset = (data_offset / 2) + comm_flags0_offset;\n\n    for(int r = 0; r < kWorldSize; r++)\n    {\n        int32x4_t* send_buffer = reinterpret_cast<int32x4_t*>(\n            buffer_ptr[r] + comm_data0_offset + rank * Codec::kRankTransmittedTileSize);\n        codec.send(send_buffer, &tA[r * Codec::kRankAtoms]);\n    }\n\n    __syncthreads();\n    if(thread < kWorldSize)\n    {\n        int r              = thread;\n        uint32_t* flag_ptr = reinterpret_cast<uint32_t*>(buffer_ptr[r] + comm_flags0_offset +\n                                                         rank * sizeof(uint32_t));\n        set_sync_flag(flag_ptr, flag_color);\n    }\n    // --------------------------------------------------------\n    // Phase-1B: Reduce the segment data from the communication buffers.\n    int32x4_t tR[Codec::kRankAtoms] = {};\n    {\n        // Read the data from the communication buffer.\n        int32x4_t* recv_buffer = reinterpret_cast<int32x4_t*>(rank_buffer + comm_data0_offset);\n        uint32_t* flag_ptr     = reinterpret_cast<uint32_t*>(rank_buffer + comm_flags0_offset);\n\n        for(int r = 0; r < kWorldSize; r++)\n        {\n            // Wait for the flags to be set.\n            if(thread == 0)\n            {\n                wait_sync_flag(&flag_ptr[r], flag_color);\n            }\n            __syncthreads();\n\n            // note: we reuse tA as temp buffer here\n            codec.recv(&recv_buffer, tA);\n\n            for(int i = 0; i < Codec::kRankAtoms; i++)\n            {\n                packed_assign_add<CommT>(&tR[i], &tA[i]);\n            }\n        }\n    }\n\n    // Phase-2: Write the reduced segment to every other rank\n    for(int r = 0; r < kWorldSize; r++)\n    {\n        int32x4_t* send_buffer = reinterpret_cast<int32x4_t*>(\n            buffer_ptr[r] + comm_data1_offset + rank * Codec::kRankTransmittedTileSize);\n        codec.send(send_buffer, tR);\n    }\n\n    __syncthreads();\n    if(thread < kWorldSize)\n    {\n        int r              = thread;\n        uint32_t* flag_ptr = reinterpret_cast<uint32_t*>(buffer_ptr[r] + comm_flags1_offset +\n                                                         rank * sizeof(uint32_t));\n        set_sync_flag(flag_ptr, flag_color);\n    }\n\n    // Phase-2: Read the gather segments from the rank's communication buffer.\n    {\n        // Read the data from the communication buffer.\n        int32x4_t* recv_buffer = reinterpret_cast<int32x4_t*>(rank_buffer + comm_data1_offset);\n        uint32_t* flag_ptr     = reinterpret_cast<uint32_t*>(rank_buffer + comm_flags1_offset);\n\n        for(int r = 0; r < kWorldSize; r++)\n        {\n            // Wait for the flags to be set.\n            if(thread == 0)\n            {\n                wait_sync_flag(&flag_ptr[r], flag_color);\n            }\n            __syncthreads();\n\n            // Gather all reduced and final rank segments into tA.\n            codec.recv(&recv_buffer, &tA[r * Codec::kRankAtoms]);\n        }\n    }\n\n    // --------------------------------------------------------\n    // Cast back if needed\n    if constexpr(cast_bf2half)\n    {\n        for(int i = 0; i < kAtoms; i++)\n        {\n            const half2* half_buf = reinterpret_cast<const half2*>(&tA[i]);\n            nv_bfloat162 bf16_buf[4];\n            #pragma unroll\n            for(int j = 0; j < 4; ++j)\n            {\n                float2 f    = __half22float2(half_buf[j]);\n                bf16_buf[j] = __float22bfloat162_rn(f);\n            }\n            tA[i] = *reinterpret_cast<const int32x4_t*>(bf16_buf);\n        }\n    }\n\n    // --------------------------------------------------------\n    // Epilogue: add residual, write residual_out, compute sum of squares\n    constexpr int kMaxRowsPerTile = kTileSize / sizeof(T) / 1; // 16384\n    // Use shared memory for rows that fit; for very small hidden_dim we might\n    // need more, but typical hidden_dims (4096, 8192) give 4 or 2 rows.\n    __shared__ float row_sq_sums[32];\n    int rows_per_tile = (hidden_dim > 0) ? (kTileSize / sizeof(T)) / hidden_dim : 1;\n\n    // Initialize shared memory\n    if(thread < 32)\n    {\n        row_sq_sums[thread] = 0.0f;\n    }\n    __syncthreads();\n\n    BufferResource res_buffer(const_cast<T*>(residual_inp), N * sizeof(T));\n    BufferResource res_out_buffer(residual_out, N * sizeof(T));\n\n    uint32_t elem_offset = block * kTileSize + thread * sizeof(int32x4_t);\n\n    for(int i = 0; i < kAtoms; i++)\n    {\n        // Load residual\n        int32x4_t res_chunk = buffer_load_dwordx4(res_buffer.descriptor, elem_offset, 0, 0);\n        T* res_vals = reinterpret_cast<T*>(&res_chunk);\n        T* red_vals = reinterpret_cast<T*>(&tA[i]);\n\n        float local_sq_sum = 0.0f;\n        int current_row = -1;\n\n        for(int lane = 0; lane < kElemsPerAtom; lane++)\n        {\n            float red_f = qr_to_float<T>(red_vals[lane]);\n            float res_f = qr_to_float<T>(res_vals[lane]);\n            float sum_f = red_f + res_f;\n            red_vals[lane] = qr_from_float<T>(sum_f);\n\n            uint32_t global_elem = (elem_offset - block * kTileSize) / sizeof(T) + lane;\n            int row_in_tile = global_elem / hidden_dim;\n\n            if(row_in_tile < rows_per_tile && row_in_tile < 32)\n            {\n                local_sq_sum += sum_f * sum_f;\n                current_row = row_in_tile;\n            }\n        }\n\n        // Write residual_out\n        buffer_store_dwordx4(tA[i], res_out_buffer.descriptor, elem_offset, 0, 0);\n\n        // Atomic add to shared memory (one per chunk since all lanes in a chunk\n        // are in the same row for typical hidden_dim >= 8)\n        if(current_row >= 0 && local_sq_sum != 0.0f)\n        {\n            atomicAdd(&row_sq_sums[current_row], local_sq_sum);\n        }\n\n        elem_offset += kAtomStride * sizeof(int32x4_t);\n    }\n\n    __syncthreads();\n\n    // Compute denom = rsqrt(mean + eps) per row\n    if(thread < rows_per_tile && thread < 32)\n    {\n        float mean = row_sq_sums[thread] / float(hidden_dim);\n        row_sq_sums[thread] = rsqrtf(mean + eps);\n    }\n    __syncthreads();\n\n    // Write output: apply RMSNorm scaling\n    BufferResource weight_buffer(const_cast<T*>(weight), hidden_dim * sizeof(T));\n    BufferResource out_buffer(output, N * sizeof(T));\n\n    elem_offset = block * kTileSize + thread * sizeof(int32x4_t);\n    for(int i = 0; i < kAtoms; i++)\n    {\n        T* sum_vals = reinterpret_cast<T*>(&tA[i]);\n        int32x4_t out_chunk;\n        T* out_vals = reinterpret_cast<T*>(&out_chunk);\n\n        for(int lane = 0; lane < kElemsPerAtom; lane++)\n        {\n            uint32_t global_elem = (elem_offset - block * kTileSize) / sizeof(T) + lane;\n            int row_in_tile = global_elem / hidden_dim;\n            int col_in_row = global_elem % hidden_dim;\n\n            float sum_f = qr_to_float<T>(sum_vals[lane]);\n            float denom = (row_in_tile < rows_per_tile && row_in_tile < 32)\n                              ? row_sq_sums[row_in_tile] : 1.0f;\n\n            // Load weight\n            T w_val;\n            // We can't easily use buffer_load for weight since it's small and indexed.\n            // Just do a direct load.\n            w_val = weight[col_in_row];\n            float w_f = qr_to_float<T>(w_val);\n\n            float norm_f = sum_f * denom * w_f;\n            out_vals[lane] = qr_from_float<T>(norm_f);\n        }\n\n        buffer_store_dwordx4(out_chunk, out_buffer.descriptor, elem_offset, 0, 0);\n        elem_offset += kAtomStride * sizeof(int32x4_t);\n    }\n}\n```\n\nWait, there's an issue with the `local_sq_sum` accumulation. {"type":"reasoning","timestamp":1784397679516,"sessionID":"ses_089a6893effeFuOe5qeP2JE8cm","part":{"id":"prt_f766367e1001kwOusIzgBVUuFP","messageID":"msg_f76635ab7001fF0TCgDQEvHrFL","sessionID":"ses_089a6893effeFuOe5qeP2JE8cm","type":"reasoning","text":"The issue is that each atom (`int32x4_t`) spans 8 elements of type `T` (since `sizeof(T)==2` and `sizeof(int32x4_t)==16`). So `first_elem / hidden_dim` is the row index for the first element in the atom, but the last element might cross into the next row if `hidden_dim` is not a multiple of `kElemsPerAtom` (8). However, the host launcher checks that `row_bytes` divides `kTileSize`, and `kTileSize = 32768`. For `hidden_dim=4096` and `sizeof(T)=2`, `row_bytes=8192`, and `kTileSize % row_bytes == 0` with `rows_per_tile = 4`. `8192 / 2 = 4096` elements per row, and each atom is 8 elements. So each atom stays within a row (since 4096 is a multiple of 8). So `row_in_tile` is indeed constant across all lanes in an atom. Good.\n\nBut our warp-level reduction adds the entire atom's `lane_sq` to `row_sq_sums[row_in_tile]`. This is correct — each warp handles multiple atoms, and each atom is fully within a single row.\n\nWait, but each warp (64 threads) processes multiple atoms. Each thread processes one atom per loop iteration. Within a warp, different threads may be processing atoms from the *same* row or *different* rows depending on the thread index. But since `first_elem = (base + thread * 16) / 2`, adjacent threads handle adjacent 8-element chunks. For `hidden_dim=4096`, a row spans 4096 elements, so a row spans `4096/8 = 512` threads. A warp is 64 threads, so all threads in a warp are within the same row. Good.\n\nWhat if `hidden_dim` is smaller? The check `row_bytes divides kTileSize` means `kTileSize / row_bytes` is integer. If `hidden_dim = 2048`, then `row_bytes = 4096`, `rows_per_tile = 8`. A row spans `2048/8 = 256` threads. A warp is 64 threads, so a warp is still within the same row. In general, `hidden_dim` is a power of 2 ≥ 512? Actually the note says \"power-of-2 hidden dims like 4096/8192 work\". The smallest power-of-2 that satisfies `row_bytes divides kTileSize` and `row_bytes ≤ kTileSize` is `hidden_dim = 512` (row_bytes=1024, rows_per_tile=32). 512/8=64 threads per row, which exactly matches a warp.
